## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws and ODE concentration dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of concentration A(t), which is the standard object modeled by chemical kinetics ODEs. With only t and A available, plausible structures are concentration-dependent rate laws (mass-action orders, autocatalysis, equilibrium relaxation) and possibly time-dependent effective rate coefficients (forcing, catalyst activation/deactivation).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption; e.g., saturated catalyst/constant flux)
- First-order decay (mass action): dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive-like kinetics, many dilute reactions)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular A+A or pseudo-second-order regimes)
- n-th order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (effective reaction order fitted from data)
- Half-order / fractional order: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 with 0 < c1 < 1 (surface/radical chain limited regimes giving non-integer order)
- Approach to equilibrium (linear relaxation): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (relaxation toward equilibrium concentration c1)
- Reversible/pseudo-first-order with constant back-flux: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 (forward loss proportional to A plus approximately constant production)
- Autocatalytic (limited) kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating production with depletion/limitation; yields sigmoidal A(t))
- Chain-branching/termination competition: dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (growth term opposed by quadratic termination)
- Time-dependent first-order (activation/deactivation): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (effective rate coefficient changes exponentially in time)
- Linear time-forced first-order: dA_dt = -c0 * (c1 + c2 * t) * A (slow drift in effective rate due to aging, ramped conditions)
- Periodically forced kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) * A (light modulation/mixing cycles causing periodic effective rate)
- Substrate/product inhibition (rational rate): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + c2 * A + A**2) (rate suppressed at high A by inhibition/complexation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Consumption of A typically implies dA_dt < 0 for A > 0; models often include an overall negative sign multiplying a nonnegative function of A.
- A straight line in log(A) vs t suggests dA_dt ∝ -A (first-order); curvature consistent with dA_dt ∝ -A**n indicates n ≠ 1.
- If A(t) approaches a nonzero plateau, include an offset equilibrium term like (A - c1) rather than pure -A**n.
- Sigmoidal A(t) or initially slow then fast change is consistent with autocatalysis (terms like A*(c1 - A) or +A - A**2).
- If the apparent rate changes systematically over time at fixed A, incorporate a time-varying effective rate coefficient k(t) multiplying A**n (e.g., exp(c*t), c0+c1*t).
- Oscillations or periodic ripples in A(t) suggest periodic forcing in the rate coefficient (sin(c*t), cos(c*t)) rather than high-degree polynomials in A.
- Strong slowing at high A can be captured by rational inhibition forms where A appears in both numerator and denominator (e.g., A/(c1 + c2*A + A**2)).
- Presence of both production and consumption channels often appears as a sum of terms with different orders/signs (e.g., +c0*A - c1*A**2 or -c0*A + c1).

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK33)
============================================================
GT: -c0*sqrt(A) - c1*A**c2 + c3*_t*sin(log(A + c4))
Candidates evaluated: 66
Matched candidate IDs: []

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.11847*sqrt(A) - 0.11847*A^2 + 0.84638*sin(log(A + 1))`

The GT contains three basis functions:
1. `sqrt(A)` (i.e., `A^(1/2)`)
2. `A^2`
3. `sin(log(A + 1))`

Key observation: The GT has `sin(log(A+1))` which is a very specific transcendental function. For a candidate to match, it must be able to produce this function exactly.

Let me categorize the candidates by their basis functions:

**Candidates with `sin` terms:** 10, 11, 24, 33, 39, 41, 42, 44, 45, 46, 47, 53
- These have `sin(A*c + c)` which is `sin` of a **linear** function of A, NOT `sin(log(A+1))`. These cannot match.

**Candidates with `log` terms:** 1, 2, 3, 5, 6, 7, 8, 9, 13, 15, 16, 20, 22, 28, 30, 31, 34, 35, 48, 49, 53
- These have `log(A*c + 1)` but NOT `sin(log(A+1))`. `log` alone cannot produce `sin(log(...))`.

**Candidates with `exp` terms:** 1, 2, 3, 13, 14, 20, 23, 33, 36, 37, 38, 43, 47, 49, 50, 51, 52, 55, 59, 60, 62, 64
- `exp` cannot produce `sin(log(...))`.

**Candidates with `A^c` (free power):** 1, 2, 12, 48, 54, 56, 57, 58, 59, 61
- `A^c` with free c can give `sqrt(A)` (set c=0.5), but still can't produce `sin(log(A+1))`.

**Candidates with rational functions, polynomials only:** 4, 17, 21, 25, 26, 27, 29, 32, 40, 63, 18, 19
- These are rational/polynomial and cannot produce `sin(log(A+1))`.

**Candidate 65:** `A*c0 + A*c1/(A*c2 + c3) + c4*log(c5*exp(A*c6) + 1) + c7/(A*c2 + c3)`
- Has `log(c5*exp(A*c6) + 1)` which is a softplus-like function, not `sin(log(...))`.

**Candidate 66:** Rational + exp terms, no sin(log(...)).

None of the candidates contain `sin(log(...))` as a basis function. The GT requires `sin(log(A+1))`, which is a composition of sin and log. No candidate has this composition. The candidates either have:
- `sin(linear in A)` - wrong argument to sin
- `log(linear in A)` - no sin wrapper
- `exp(linear in A)` - completely different
- Polynomials/rational functions - cannot produce transcendental oscillations of this type

Since `sin(log(A+1))` cannot be expressed as any finite combination of polynomials, exponentials, simple logs, or `sin(linear)` functions, none of the candidates can match the GT.

Let me verify: Could any candidate numerically approximate the GT well enough to be considered equivalent? No - the problem asks for **mathematical equivalence**, not approximation.
